Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                                 Module B, slide 11 of 32

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
        Sun Learning Services

        Stable Dependencies Principle

Stability means a component is fixed, permanent, and
unvarying.

    · Business services and entities tend to be stable.
    · Entities tend to be more stable than services.
    · UI components tend to change.
    · Utilities tend to be stable.

SDP (and CCP) compliment the Tiers partitioning of SunTone
AM:

    · Components closer to the resource tier tend to be more
         stable.

    · Components closer to the client tier tend to be less stable.

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module B, slide 12 of 32

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
Sun Learning Services

    Stable Abstractions Principle

   "Stable packages should be abstract packages." (Knoernschild
   page 31)

«Java package»  «Java package»

 com.bayview     com.bayview
.web.makeresv      .services

   MakeResvCtl     «interface»

                 ResvService

                                                                                                 «Java package»

                                                                                                  com.bayview
                                                                                                 .services.impl

                                                                                              ResvServiceImpl

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module B, slide 13 of 32

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
        Sun Learning Services

         Stable Abstractions Principle

This principle is an extension of the Dependency Inversion
Principle for classes and components.

    · Less stable packages should depend on abstractions
        within another package, rather than concretions.

    · Abstract classes and interfaces tend to change less
        frequently than their implementation classes.

    · The formula for determining abstractness of a package
        is:
                                   A = -NN----ac-

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module B, slide 14 of 32

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
  Sun Learning Services

Isolating Subsystems and Frameworks

      subsystem ­ "A collection of modules, some of which are visible to
      other subsystems and other of which are hidden." (Booch OOAD
      page 519)

      framework ­ "A collection of classes that provide a set of services for
      a particular domain; a framework thus exports a number of individual
      classes and mechanisms that clients can use or adapt." (Booch OOAD
      page 514)

· Subsystems and frameworks are usually placed in their
    own package.

· Only public classes or interfaces are visible outside of
    the package.

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module B, slide 15 of 32

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
        Sun Learning Services

   Developing a Package Structure for the
                   Solution Model

From the package dependency principles, these are a few
guidelines for creating a package structure:

    · Group components of each tier into their own package.
         For example, the business services and entities should be
         in their own package.

    · Within a tier, group components that change together
         into their own package. For example, the client-tier
         components for a web application might be grouped
         together.

    · Group interfaces of a set of services into a package and
         their implementation into another package.

    · Isolate subsystems into their own packages.

   MyClass              public class MyClass {
                           // members
  AbsClass
                        }
            {abstract}
                        public abstract class AbsClass {
  «interface»              // members

MyInterface             }

                        public interface MyInterface {
                           // members

                        }

                           public class A {

              A               // members

                           }

                           public class B extends A {

              B               // members

                           }

              «interface»  public interface A {
                              // members
                    A
                           }
                    B
                           public class B implements A {
                              // members

                           }

                      Attributes

UML Syntax:
[visibility] name [multiplicity] [: type] [= init-
value] [{property-string}]

                                                        Customer

                                               -firstName : String {frozen}
                                               -lastName : String {frozen}
                                               -address : Address = new Address()
                                               -phone [1..2] : PhoneNumber = null

                                     public class Customer {
                                         private final String firstName;
                                         private final String lastName;
                                         private Address address = new Address();
                                         private PhoneNumber[] phone = null;

                                     }

   · Visibility:

UML Accessibility
Symbol Keyword

~  default

-  private

   · Class scope:

          MyClass         public class MyClass {
                             private int instanceVar;
   -instanceVar : int        private static int classVar;
   -classVar : int
                          }

Associations

Associations between classes are usually implemented as an
attribute:

Room                                                                                          Property

public class Room {
   private Property property;

}

Important features:

    · Navigation
    · Multiplicity
    · Qualified associations
    · Aggregation and composition

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                           Module B, slide 24 of 32

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
Sun Learning Services

Navigation

The navigation arrow specifies which class must implement
the association and its access method.

    · Unidirectional:

                                      Room                                                         Property

                              public class Room {                                             public class Property {
                                 private Property property;                                      //members

                              }                                                               }

· Bidirectional:

        Room                                                                                       Property

public class Room {                                                                           public class Property {
   private Property property;                                                                    private Room room;

}                                                                                             }

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                                          Module B, slide 25 of 32

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
        Sun Learning Services

               Association Methods

Proper encapsulation also recommends keeping the
association instance variable private and providing public
access and mutator methods:

Room                                                                                          Property

-property:Property

+getProperty():Property
+setProperty(:Property)

public class Room {
   private Property property;
   public Property getProperty() {
       return property;
   }
   public void setProperty(Property p) {
       property = p;
   }

}

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                           Module B, slide 26 of 32

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
Sun Learning Services

Association Multiplicity

Use arrays or collections to hold multiple associated objects:

                           1                                                                  1..*  Room
Property

-rooms:Collection

+getRooms():Iterator
+addRoom(:Room)
+removeRoom(:Room)

import java.util.*;
public class Property {

   private Collection rooms = new HashSet();
   public Iterator getRooms() {

       return rooms.iterator();
   }
   public void addRoom(Room r) {

       rooms.add(r);
   }
   public void removeRoom(Room r) {

       rooms.remove(r);
   }
}

Qualified Associations

A many-to-many association can be qualified by an integer
index. For example:

                    1  1
Property idx:int                  Room

import java.util.*;
public class Property {

   private List rooms = new ArrayList();
   public Room getRoom(int idx) {

       return (Room) rooms.get(idx);
   }
   public void addRoom(int idx, Room r) {

       rooms.add(idx, r);
   }
   public void removeRoom(int idx) {

       rooms.remove(idx);
   }
}

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module B, slide 28 of 32

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
        Sun Learning Services

              Qualified Associations

A qualified association may also use a non-integer key to
perform the lookup operation. For example:

                    1  1
Property name                     Room

import java.util.*;
public class Property {

   private Map rooms = new HashMap();
   public Room getRoom(String name) {

       return (Room) rooms.get(name);
   }
   public void addRoom(Room r) {

       rooms.put(r.getName(), r);
   }
   public void removeRoom(Room r) {

       rooms.remove(r.getName());
   }
}

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module B, slide 29 of 32

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
        Sun Learning Services

                    Aggregation

The parts of an aggregation may be shared outside the
aggregate class:

PolyLine  2..*
                      Point

import java.util.*;
public class PolyLine {

  private List points = new LinkedList();
  public Iterator getPoints() {

     return points.iterator();
  }
  public void addPoint(Point p) {

     points.add(p);
  }
  public void removePoint(Point p) {

     points.remove(p);
  }
}

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module B, slide 30 of 32

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
Sun Learning Services

          Composition

The parts of a composition must not be exposed outside the
composite class:

                       2..*

PolyLine                                                                                      Point

import java.util.*;
public class PolyLine {

   private List points = new LinkedList();
   // no iterator method
   public void addPoint(int x, int y) {

       points.add(new Point(x,y));
   }
   public void removePoint(int x, int y) {

       DUMMY_POINT.setX(x);
       DUMMY_POINT.setY(y);
       points.remove(DUMMY_POINT);
   }
   private final static DUMMY_POINT = new Point(0,0);
}

            Defining System Testing

            The test workflow is meant to "verify that the system correctly
            implements its specification." (Jacobson, Booch, and Rumbaugh
            page 55)

There are numerous tests that could be performed:

    · Unit
    · Integration
    · Functional
    · Regression
    · Load
    · Boundary condition
    · Usability

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module C, slide 4 of 14

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
  Sun Learning Services

                   Unit Tests

      "A test written from the perspective of the programmer." (Beck
      page 179)

· Unit tests verify the behavior of individual
    components.

· Unit tests are usually written by developers.

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module C, slide 5 of 14

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
  Sun Learning Services

              Integration Tests

      "Integration testing tests multiple components that have each received
      prior and separate unit testing." (Whittaker page 77)

· Integration tests verify the behavior across multiple
    components, subsystems, and complete systems.

· Integration tests are usually written by testing
    professionals or by the development team.

· Integration tests should be built incrementally just as
    the system is built incrementally.

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module C, slide 6 of 14

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
  Sun Learning Services

              Functional Tests

      "Most functional tests are written as black box tests working off a
      functional specification." (Chillarege page 3)

· Functional tests verify the behavior of the (complete)
    system from the perspective of the user.

· Functional tests must be written by testing
    professionals in conjunction with the user community
    (if possible).

· Functional tests are based on the use cases of the
    system plus variations of all scenarios.

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module C, slide 7 of 14

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
        Sun Learning Services

         Developing a Functional Test

A function test is written based on a use case of the system.

    1. Identify the inputs for the test based on the inputs
        specified in the use case scenario.

    2. Specify the results of the test.
    3. Specify the conditions under which the test must be

         performed.
    4. Write variations on this test to check failure

         processing, boundary conditions, and so on.

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module C, slide 8 of 14

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
        Sun Learning Services

       Identifying Functional Test Inputs

Functional test inputs include all data that must be entered
into the system through the user interface.

Example: (E1: Create Reservation)

    · The HotelApp is running with the Santa Cruz bed and
        breakfast.

    · The begin and end dates of the reservation are January
        31, 2002 and February 5, 2002, respectively.

    · The type of room requested is double.
    · The Blue room is selected from the room search.
    · Enter Jane Googol into the customer search.
    · Enter a valid credit card number.

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module C, slide 9 of 14

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
        Sun Learning Services

      Identifying Functional Test Results

Functional test results include any output generated by the
system as well as any persistent state change in the system.

Example: (E1: Create Reservation)

    · A new reservation will exist for Jane Googol.
    · The state of this reservation will be "confirmed."
    · The reservation has an association with the Blue room

        (and only the Blue room).
    · The payment entity for this reservation records the

        correct credit card number.

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module C, slide 10 of 14

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
        Sun Learning Services

    Identifying Functional Test Conditions

Functional test conditions include the existence of specific
entities in the database and the existence of stubs for external
systems and their data.

Example: (E1: Create Reservation)

    · The database contains the Santa Cruz bed and breakfast
         property and is associated with the Blue room, which is a
         double.

    · Jane Googol is a valid customer in the database.
    · A stub exists for the external credit card authorization

         system with data for test credit cards.
    · No other concurrent tests must interact with that credit card

         account.

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module C, slide 11 of 14

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
        Sun Learning Services

       Creating Functional Test Variants

Tests variants are based on a use case scenario and explore the
state space of the system.

Example: (E1: Create Reservation)

    · Include a variant in which there are multiple customer
        entities for a single name; for example, John Smith.

    · Include a variant in which the a room search produces
        no available rooms.

    · Include a variant in which the credit card is not
        authorized and the customer presents a second credit
        card.

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module C, slide 12 of 14

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
  Sun Learning Services

        Documenting Test Cases

· All test cases should be stored in a Test Plan document.
· Each functional test must trace back to a use case in the

    SRS document.
· If the system is large, then the Test Plan document can

    be split up separate documents--one for each major
    increment of the system.
· The Test Plan must be approved by the customer.
· Other types of tests (such as load and usability tests)
    are usually documented separately.

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module C, slide 13 of 14

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
  Sun Learning Services

                   Summary

· Testing is critical to the success of a software project.
· Except for unit and integration testing, no tests should

    be developed and performed by the development
    team.
· Functional tests are developed from the system's use
    case scenarios.
· Functional test variants are created to test boundary
    conditions and system robustness.

Explaining the Deployment Workflow

Deployment of the software solution is usually performed by
the system administration team of the client company. The
development team usually only has a consulting role.

Here are some of the many possible activities:

    · Purchase necessary hardware and software.
    · Construct the networking infrastructure.
    · Install the third-party and custom software.
    · Migrate legacy data to new system (if necessary).
    · Test the installation.
    · Train the staff.
    · Go live.

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module D, slide 4 of 12

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
  Sun Learning Services

    Using the Deployment Diagram

· The Deployment diagram of the system is the
    architect's vision of how the system should be
    deployed.

· The Deployment diagram should provide both the
    structure of the network and the set of software
    components.

· The "descriptive" Deployment diagram (created in the
    Elaboration phase) needs to be elaborated with details
    in the "instance" Deployment diagram before
    deployment can proceed.

Object-Oriented Analysis and Design Using UML                                                 Module D, slide 5 of 12

Copyright 2010 Sun Microsystems, Inc. All Rights Reserved. Sun Learning Services, Revision E
        Sun Learning Services

Creating an Instance Deployment Diagram

Creating an instance Deployment diagram from a descriptive
Deployment diagrams requires adding the following features:

    · Detailed network configuration
    · Detailed hardware configuration
    · Detailed software configuration

                   Summary

· The Deployment workflow takes the system
    implementation into production.

· The Deployment diagram specifies how the system is
    to be deployed in the production configuration.

· An instance Deployment diagram elaborates the
    descriptor Deployment diagram by clearly specifying
    the configuration of:
    · Networks
    · Machines
    · Software components
